import bark.generation

[2023-05-02 19:04:02] 636706883859906562: ```python
import re

def process_line(line, characters):
    pattern = r"\{([^}]+)\}:?"
    match = re.search(pattern, line)

    if match:
        actor = match.group(1)
        line = re.sub(pattern, "", line).strip()
        character_voice = characters.get(actor, {}).get("voice", None)
    else:
        character_voice = None

    return line, character_voice

actors = {
    "MAN": {"voice": "hi_speaker_1"},
    "WOMAN": {"voice": "hi_speaker_5"},
}

prompt = """{MAN}: Hello, lady!
{WOMAN} Hello, sir!
"""

# Then, to use it:
lines = prompt.split("\n")

for line in lines:
    line_segment, character_voice = process_line(line, actors)
    ...generate_audio(line_segment, history_prompt=character_voice)..
```
[2023-05-02 19:04:51] 636706883859906562: there is a simple example if anyone wants to try to do it in a Colab Notebook or something, though obviously you'll need to decide what you do with those waveforms. you can concatenate and use Audio for an AudioSegment, i think.

[2023-05-03 19:58:07] 456226577798135808: @Jonathan Fly - I fixed the encoding error with some code changes. It was related to the logger.

```python
class Logger:
    def __init__(self, filename):
        self.terminal = sys.stdout
        self.log = open(filename, "w", encoding="utf-8")

    def write(self, message):
        self.terminal.write(message)
        self.log.write(message)

    def flush(self):
        self.terminal.flush()
        self.log.flush()

    def isatty(self):
        return False


sys.stdout = io.TextIOWrapper(sys.stdout.buffer, encoding='utf-8', errors='replace', newline='', line_buffering=True)
sys.stderr = io.TextIOWrapper(sys.stderr.buffer, encoding='utf-8', errors='replace', newline='', line_buffering=True)

sys.stdout = Logger("gradio_terminal_ouput.log")```

```python
def read_logs():
    sys.stdout.flush()
    with open("gradio_terminal_ouput.log", "r", encoding="utf-8") as f:
        return f.read()```

[2023-05-03 20:50:21] 636706883859906562: i'm doing that in my Discord bot by editing the message with the new progress bar contents every 20%
[2023-05-03 20:51:37] 636706883859906562: you have to capture each frame of stdout changes and check for the current % value via regular expressions, you can keep track of which stage it's on and fudge the overall % output so that it takes each stage into consideration before reaching 100% instead of eg. counting to 100% for both stages, so that when it hits the end of the stage 1 it's only at 50%

[2023-05-03 20:55:38] 636706883859906562: it doesn't matter
[2023-05-03 20:55:39] 614946962139250711: so I google that and it was like, well you CAN deal with that
[2023-05-03 20:55:43] 614946962139250711: but it sounded messy
[2023-05-03 20:55:44] 636706883859906562: it can chain itself
[2023-05-03 20:55:52] 614946962139250711: like the bars reset each other
[2023-05-03 20:56:04] 636706883859906562: pytorch in general uses tqdm and then bark uses tqdm on top and then i do:
```python
import re, asyncio, logging
from discord_tron_client.classes.discord_progress_bar import DiscordProgressBar
from discord_tron_client.classes.hardware import HardwareInfo

class TqdmCapture:
    def __init__(self, progress_bar: DiscordProgressBar, loop):
        self.progress_bar = progress_bar
        self.loop = loop
        self.output_file = "/tmp/tqdm_output.txt"
        self.hardware_info = HardwareInfo()
        self.gpu_power_consumption = 0.0 # Store GPU power use here, since it's inside the loop.
        # Start below zero so that a progress of zero will begin the bar.
        self.progress = -1

    def write(self, s: str):
        test_string = s.strip()
        if test_string != "":
            with open(self.output_file, 'a') as f:
                f.write(s)

            match = re.search(r'\b(\d+)%\|', s)
            if match:
                progress = int(match.group(1))
                if progress <= self.progress:
                    # If we have anything less than what we started with, don't send.
                    return
                self.progress = progress
                    
                if progress >= 50 and progress <= 60:
                    # Record GPU power use around 60% progress.
                    self.gpu_power_consumption = self.hardware_info.get_gpu_power_consumption()
                asyncio.run_coroutine_threadsafe(self.progress_bar.update_progress_bar(progress), self.loop)

    def flush(self):
        with open(self.output_file, 'a') as f:
            f.flush()
```

[2023-05-03 21:08:04] 636706883859906562: ```python

    def __init__(
        self,
        choices: List[str],
        type: str = "value",
        default: Optional[str] = None,
        label: Optional[str] = None,
        optional: bool = False,
    ):
        """
        Parameters:
        choices (List[str]): list of options to select from.
        type (str): Type of value to be returned by component. "value" returns the string of the choice selected, "index" returns the index of the choice selected.
        default (str): default value selected in dropdown. If None, no value is selected by default.
        label (str): component name in interface.
        optional (bool): this parameter is ignored.
        """
        warnings.warn(
            "Usage of gradio.inputs is deprecated, and will not be supported in the future, please import your component from gradio.components",
            DeprecationWarning,
        )
        super().__init__(
            choices=choices,
            type=type,
            value=default,
            label=label,
            optional=optional,
        )
```

[2023-05-04 15:24:05] 636706883859906562: it takes many tries to get one that even just says anything let alone a high quality output. you can generate 100s of voice output with the one wav you present it. and due to the GPT nature of this model, it will produce a varying output each time. [2023-05-04 15:24:37] 636706883859906562: you can eventually generate a pretty good one. `announcer.npz` is a great voice.

[2023-05-06 03:17:58] 614946962139250711: Do you mean a random voice, or an .npz file? You can save all your random voices, but it's not done by default
[2023-05-06 03:19:35] 614946962139250711: api.save_as_prompt()
[2023-05-06 03:21:33] 392888217222774786: A random voice generated using the generate_audio(text_prompt) without the history_prompt parameter. I want to get the last random voice and make it the standard for the next prompts. Is it possible?
[2023-05-06 03:23:59] 614946962139250711: Yes, call generate_audio with output_full = True, 
```full_generation, audio_arr = api.generate_audio(output_full = True)
api.save_as_prompt("myfile.npz", full_generation)```

[2023-05-14 00:32:42] 614946962139250711: I think I've got a quite a few voices now that are equal or maybe even better than eleven, took a recent diversion and now busy with real life stuff, but I'll collect and post a ton eventually. The trick to actually being *better* than eleven is using multiple variants of the same .npz file, and picking the right one in the right context. But I don't have a automated system or anything yet. Nothing fancy, just keeping a small handful of versions and then choosing the best one for a particular segment.
[2023-05-14 00:36:46] 614946962139250711: This is all low hanging un-tapped fruit. To mix my metaphors. Don't just generate one speaker, make a bunch of versions. Emotions, speed. [2023-05-18 00:17:13] 546862623581536284: Just from reading the source code, for the "high-level" generation call `generate_audio`,  `text_temp` controls the "diversity" (basically, randomness in which token is seen as best) in translation of text to semantic tokens, and `waveform_temp` does the same thing for generation of coarse and fine audio tokens from the semantic tokens. (`text_temp` gets passed as just plain `temp` in `text_to_semantic`, `waveform_temp` gets passed as `temp` to `semantic_to_waveform` and from there to the same parameter in both `generate_coarse` and `generate_fine`.) There's more tuning available if you bypass `generate_audio` and call the lower level routines directly, `top_k` and `top_p`(in both `generate_text_semantic` and `generate_coarse`) are for different strategies besides just picking the "best" token after applying the temperature parameter, and `generate_text_semantic` has other tuning parameters that all seem to relate to when to stop (`min_eos_p`, `max_gen_duration_s`, `allow_early_stop`) while `generate_coarse` has a few that seem to relate to different aspects of how context effects token generation, `max_coarse_history` and `sliding_window_len`.) But, beyond an intuition that `text_temp` ought to have some effect on consistency of _what_ the voice says and `waveform_temp` on consistency of _how it sounds_ saying it...

[2023-05-19 08:51:32] 614946962139250711: Well if the seal on voice cloning is broken anyway, I suppose I may as well post some of the funniest stuff. It's not just Trevor Noah speaking in a French accent. I was gonna make a YouTube video but I keep getting distracting. The YouTube would be about the process for making these, the voice cloning is surprisingly quite different than Mylo's reverse semantic model, extremely convoluted and weird. But fascinating. A lot of experiments and I didn't bother automating it, since I figured the real method like Mylo would be along soon enough, and should be more general purpose. It takes at least a couple hours of me actively poking and experimenting, listening, writing a new notebook cell based one some guesses for the next generation, listening again, over and over to clone a voice, so I only made about 10 clear clones. Maybe 10 more half-way done noisy one, just to test it works on more extreme voices. (Yes but was harder.) I did think about automating it, but this is really a totally insane way to do this compared to the 'right' way, there's no point. I was just shocked and fascinated that it works. I've looked at soooo many strings of raw token IDs sometimes I think I can hear a raw semantic model output in my own head, without decoding it, like a piece of sheet music. (Not really of course. Also it's got a wide range since the coarse matters too. Fine is basically irrelevant though.)

[2023-05-24 13:01:37] 857874780509700098: import os
os.environ["SUNO_OFFLOAD_CPU"] = 'TRUE'
os.environ["SUNO_USE_SMALL_MODELS"] = 'TRUE'
os.environ["KMP_DUPLICATE_LIB_OK"]="TRUE"

from bark import SAMPLE_RATE, generate_audio, preload_models
from scipy.io.wavfile import write as write_wav
from IPython.display import Audio

# download and load all models
preload_models()

text_prompt = """
    I have a silky smooth voice, and today I will tell you about 
    the exercise regimen of the common sloth.
"""
text_prompt = "你好吗，我不知道我知识是否渊博"
audio_array = generate_audio(text=text_prompt, history_prompt="v2/myself")
print(audio_array)
# save audio to disk
write_wav("./tmp.wav", SAMPLE_RATE, audio_array)
  
# play text in notebook
Audio(audio_array, rate=SAMPLE_RATE)

def load_npz(filename):
    with np.load(filename, allow_pickle=True) as data:
        return {key: data[key] for key in data}

history_prompt = load_npz("./voices/en_music_female_test.npz")
```
